<td colspan="2" style="text-align:left; vertical-align:middle; padding:0 0 0 3px; white-space:nowrap; border: 0px !important;"><span style="font-size:90%;padding-left:3px"><i><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Northeast Regional</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amtrak_Virginia" title="Amtrak Virginia">Virginia</a></i></span></td>

<p>The <i><b>Acela Express</b></i> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>ə-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">SEL</span></span></b>-ə</i></a></span>; colloquially abbreviated to <i><b>Acela</b></i>) is <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>'s flagship service along the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a> (NEC) in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeast_United_States" title="Northeast United States">Northeast United States</a> between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_DC" title="Washington DC">Washington DC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> via 14 intermediate stops including <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. The route contains segments of <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail#Americas" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a>, and Acela Express trains are the fastest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_terminology#T" title="Rail terminology">trainsets</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>; they attain 150 mph (240 km/h) on 28 miles (45 km) of the route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTtimeli_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTtimeli-8">[8]</a></sup> Acela trains use <a href="/wiki/Tilting_train" title="Tilting train">tilting</a> technology, which helps control lateral <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centrifugal_force_(rotating_reference_frame)" title="Centrifugal force (rotating reference frame)">centrifugal forces</a>, allowing the train to travel at higher speeds on the sharply curved NEC without disturbing passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tilt_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-tilt-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Acela</i> operates along routes that are also used by freight and slower regional passenger traffic, and only reaches the <a href="/wiki/Rail_speed_limits_in_the_United_States" title="Rail speed limits in the United States">maximum allowed speed</a> of the tracks along some sections, with the fastest peak speed along segments between <a href="/wiki/Mansfield,_Massachusetts" title="Mansfield, Massachusetts">Mansfield, Massachusetts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Rhode_Island" title="Richmond, Rhode Island">Richmond, Rhode Island</a>. The high-speed operation occurs mostly along the 226-mile (364 km) route from New York's <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Station_(New_York_City)" title="Pennsylvania Station (New York City)">Penn Station</a> to Washington DC's <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Union Station (Washington, D.C.)">Union Station</a>, with a fastest scheduled time of 2 hours and 45 minutes and an average speed of 82 mph (132 km/h), including time spent at intermediate stops. Over this route, <i>Acela</i> and the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Northeast Regional</a> line captured a 75% share of air/train commuters between New York and Washington in 2011, up from 37% in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hassles_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-hassles-10">[10]</a></sup> Due to this competition, one airline canceled service between Washington and New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baltsuntest_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-baltsuntest-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>On other portions <i>Acela</i> is limited by both traffic and infrastructure. On the 231-mile (372 km) section from Boston's <a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">South Station</a> to New York's Penn Station, the scheduled time is 3 hours and 40 minutes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hassles_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-hassles-10">[10]</a></sup> or an average speed of 63 miles per hour (101 km/h). Along this section, <i>Acela</i> has still captured 54% share of the combined train and air market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-1-Aug-2009_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-1-Aug-2009-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhI-8Dec13_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-PhI-8Dec13-14">[14]</a></sup> The entire 457-mile (735 km) route from Boston to Washington takes 7 hours,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Acela_Express_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Acela_Express-2">[2]</a></sup> at an average of around 65 miles per hour (105 km/h).</p>
<p><i>Acela</i> carried more than 3.4 million passengers in fiscal year 2015;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY15_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-FY15-1">[1]</a></sup> second only to the slower and cheaper <i><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Northeast Regional</a></i>, which had over 8 million passengers in FY 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY15_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-FY15-1">[1]</a></sup> Its 2015 revenue of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>585 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY15_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-FY15-1">[1]</a></sup> was 25% of Amtrak's total. (Another 25% came from Northeast Regional traffic, and roughly 25% each for long-distance trains and state-supported corridor services throughout the rest of the country).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY15_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-FY15-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY2012_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FY2012-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The present <i>Acela Express</i> equipment will be replaced by new <a href="/wiki/Avelia_Liberty" title="Avelia Liberty">Avelia Liberty</a> trainsets beginning in 2021, with all current trains to retire by the end of 2022. The new trainsets, manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>, will have 30% higher seating capacity than the current trains. The new fleet will have 28 trains versus the current 20, allowing for hourly New York-Boston service all day and half-hourly New York-Washington service at peak hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the success of Japan's newly inaugurated <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">Shinkansen</a> network, the <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_Ground_Transportation_Act_of_1965" title="High Speed Ground Transportation Act of 1965">High Speed Ground Transportation Act of 1965</a> authorized the U.S. government to explore the creation of high-speed rail, which resulted in the introduction of <i><a href="/wiki/Metroliner_(train)" title="Metroliner (train)">Metroliner</a></i> trains, the predecessor to <i>Acela</i>. During the 1980s the US <a href="/wiki/Federal_Railroad_Administration" title="Federal Railroad Administration">Federal Railroad Administration</a> explored the possibilities of <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_the_United_States" title="High-speed rail in the United States">high-speed rail in the United States</a>. On December 18, 1991, five potential high speed rail corridors were authorized ("Intermodal Surface Transportation Efficiency Act of 1991 (ISTEA) (PL 102-240)") including the Northeast Corridor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronology_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-chronology-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amtrak asked railway equipment manufacturers to submit proposals. An <a href="/wiki/X_2000#Overseas_appearances" title="X 2000">X 2000 train was leased</a> from Sweden for test runs from October 1992 to January 1993. It was operated from Washington DC to New York City from February to May and August to September 1993. <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> showed the <a href="/wiki/ICE_1" title="ICE 1">ICE 1</a> train from Germany, organizing the <a href="/wiki/ICE_1#ICE_train_North_America_tour" title="ICE 1">ICE Train North America Tour</a> which started to operate on the Northeast Corridor on July 3, 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etr-1993-11-756_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-etr-1993-11-756-18">[18]</a></sup> This testing allowed Amtrak to define a set of specifications that went into a public tender in October 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTtimeli_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYTtimeli-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Building_and_development">Building and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Building and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2304" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg/220px-Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg/330px-Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg/440px-Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Northbound_Acela_at_Prospect_Park_station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Northbound Acela on the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a> south of Philadelphia, showing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superelevation" title="Superelevation">superelevation</a> of the tracks.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On March 9, 1999, Amtrak unveiled its plan for a high-speed train, the <i>Acela Express</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-19">[19]</a></sup> Twenty new trains were to run on the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-overview-20">[20]</a></sup> Several changes were made to the corridor to make it suitable for the <i>Acela</i>. The Northend Electrification Project extended existing electrification from <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven</a> to Boston to complete the <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_system" title="Railway electrification system">overhead power supply</a> along the 454-mile (731 km) route, and several grade crossings were improved or removed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-overview_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-overview-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inventory_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-inventory-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 1994, Amtrak requested bids from train manufacturers for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trainset" title="Trainset">trainset</a> that could reach 150 miles per hour (240 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTtimeli_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYTtimeli-8">[8]</a></sup> A joint project of <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a> (75%) and GEC Alsthom (now <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>) (25%) was selected in March 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTtimeli_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-NYTtimeli-8">[8]</a></sup> An inaugural VIP run of the <i>Acela</i> came on November 17, 2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> followed by the first revenue run on December 11, a few months after the intended date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 2005, Amtrak's share of the common-carrier market between New York and Boston had reached 40%, from 18% pre-Acela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> With the increasing popularity of the faster, modern <i>Acela Express</i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metroliner_(Amtrak)" title="Metroliner (Amtrak)">Metroliner</a></i> service was phased out in late 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trainsmag_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-trainsmag-27">[27]</a></sup> To meet the demand, more <i>Acela</i> services were added in September 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> By August 2008 crowding had become noticeable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 2011, the Acela fleet had reached half of its designed service life. Amtrak proposed several replacement options, including one as part of its <i>A Vision for High-Speed Rail in the Northeast Corridor</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In 2011, Amtrak announced that forty new Acela coaches would be ordered in 2012 to increase capacity on existing trainsets. The existing trains would have received two more coaches, lengthening the trainsets from a 1-6-1 configuration to 1-8-1 (power car - passenger cars - power car). The longer trainsets would have required the modifications of the Acela maintenance facilities in Boston, New York and Washington. The first of the stretched trainsets was to have entered service in <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> This plan was cancelled in 2012 in favor of replacing, rather than refurbishing, the Acela fleet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2014, Amtrak issued a request for proposals on 28 or more new model Acela trainsets, in a combined order with the <a href="/wiki/California_High-Speed_Rail_Authority" title="California High-Speed Rail Authority">California High-Speed Rail Authority</a>. These bids were due May 17, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> After discussions with manufacturers, Amtrak and the California High Speed Rail Authority concluded their needs were too disparate for common rolling stock and decided not to pursue the joint option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost">Cost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cost">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Amtrak's original contract with the Bombardier-Alstom consortium was for the delivery of 20 trainsets (6 coaches each, with power cars at front and rear) for $800 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> By 2004, Amtrak had settled contract disputes with the consortium, paying a total of $1.2 billion for the 20 trainsets plus 15 extra high-speed locomotives and the construction of maintenance facilities in Boston, New York, and Washington.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramstack_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ramstack-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euronext.com_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-euronext.com-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Acela Express's fastest schedule between New York and Washington DC was 2 hours and 45 minutes in 2012. $450 million was allotted by President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s administration to replace catenary and upgrade signals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> between <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">Trenton</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick,_New_Jersey" title="New Brunswick, New Jersey">New Brunswick</a>, which will allow speeds of 160 mph (257 km/h) over 20-mile (32 km) runs after 2016. This section of track holds the record for the highest speed by a train in the US, which is 170.8 mph (274.9 km/h), achieved in a test run by the U.S./Canada-built <a href="/wiki/UAC_TurboTrain" title="UAC TurboTrain">UAC TurboTrain</a> on December 20, 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In practice, the Acela's speed depends more on local restrictions along its corridor than on its trainset. In addition to speed restrictions through urban areas, the Acela's corridor includes several speed restrictions below 60–80 mph (97–129 km/h) over older bridges, or through tunnels a century old or more. Altogether, Amtrak has identified 224 bridges along Acela's route that are beyond their design life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding">Branding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Branding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg/220px-Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg/330px-Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg/440px-Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Acela_Regional_in_Boston_South_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <i>Acela Regional</i> train at <a href="/wiki/South_Station" title="South Station">South Station</a>, Boston in 2002</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Acela</i> name was announced on March 9, 1999, as a part of the original announcement of the service itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-annou_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-annou-42">[42]</a></sup> Amtrak originally intended for this move to be part of a <a href="/wiki/Rebranding" title="Rebranding">rebranding</a> of the majority of their Northeast services,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> forming three levels: <i>Acela Express</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Acela Regional</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Clocker_(train)#Naming" title="Clocker (train)">Acela Commuter</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The branding team based the name "Acela" on the ideas of <a href="/wiki/Acceleration" title="Acceleration">acceleration</a> and excellence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were then three classes of trains on the Northeast Corridor (and its extension south to <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">Newport News, Virginia</a>)— Philadelphia-New York <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clocker_(Amtrak)" title="Clocker (Amtrak)">Clockers</a></i>, the express <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metroliner_(Amtrak)" title="Metroliner (Amtrak)">Metroliners</a></i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Umbrella_term" title="Umbrella term">umbrella term</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NortheastDirect" title="NortheastDirect">NortheastDirect</a></i>, applied to other trains on the corridor (in addition to unique names assigned to each departure). <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_Service_(Amtrak)" title="Empire Service (Amtrak)">Empire Service</a></i> trains used the <a href="/wiki/Empire_Corridor" title="Empire Corridor">Empire Corridor</a> from New York City to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls_(NY)" title="Niagara Falls (NY)">Niagara Falls</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Keystone_Service" title="Keystone Service">Keystone Service</a></i> ran along the <a href="/wiki/Keystone_Corridor" title="Keystone Corridor">Keystone Corridor</a> from Philadelphia to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harrisburg_(PA)" title="Harrisburg (PA)">Harrisburg</a>.</p>
<p>The <i>Acela Regional</i> name was first applied to <i>NortheastDirect</i> trains 130–133 on January 31, 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Those trains, 130 and 131 running weekdays only and 132 and 133 running every day, were the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway_electrification" title="Railway electrification">electrified</a> trains to run on the full Northeast Corridor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> As more trains were electrified, they too were rebranded. In 2003, due to confusion between the lower-speed <i>Acela Regional</i> trains and the <i>Acela Express</i>, the <i>Acela</i> branding was removed from the <i>NortheastDirect</i> service (now the <i><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Northeast Regional</a></i>) and the <i>Acela Commuter</i> had its name changed back to the <i>Clocker</i> for a similar reason and ultimately discontinued on October 28, 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Engineering">Engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Engineering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First-generation_train_design">First-generation train design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: First-generation train design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Acela_overhead_view.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1900" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Acela_overhead_view.jpg/170px-Acela_overhead_view.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Acela_overhead_view.jpg/255px-Acela_overhead_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Acela_overhead_view.jpg/340px-Acela_overhead_view.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Acela_overhead_view.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Overhead view of an Acela power car in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>; an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MBTA" title="MBTA">MBTA</a> <a href="/wiki/Orange_Line_(MBTA)" title="Orange Line (MBTA)">Orange Line</a> subway train is also visible in the background.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first-generation <i>Acela</i> trainset is a unique set of vehicles designed specifically to satisfy governmental rolling stock requirements established primarily by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Railroad_Administration" title="Federal Railroad Administration">Federal Railroad Administration</a> (FRA). This includes the ability to withstand a collision with a freight train at speed without collapsing. Most manufacturers which bid on the Acela were unable to meet the structural requirements, due to increased costs and complications for the manufacture of the trains, and the need for manufacturers to make significant engineering changes to their standard designs. In the end, only three qualified bidders remained: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABB" title="ABB">ABB</a> (Swiss manufacturer of the <a href="/wiki/X_2000" title="X 2000">X 2000</a> train), <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> (manufacturer of the German <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a>), and a consortium of <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a> (manufacturer of the LRC trains) and <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a> (manufacturer of the French <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The design, using identical 6,200 horsepower (4,600 kW) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Speed_Electric_Locomotive" title="High Speed Electric Locomotive">power cars</a> at each end which operate on a voltage of 11,000 volts <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">AC</a>, and either 25 or 60 <a href="/wiki/Hertz" title="Hertz">Hz</a> frequency, derives several components from the TGV,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perren.2C_Brian_p156_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perren.2C_Brian_p156-54">[54]</a></sup> such as the third-generation TGV's traction system (including the four asynchronous AC motors per power car, rectifiers, inverters, and regenerative braking), the trucks/bogies structure (a long wheelbase dual transom H frame welded steel with outboard mounted tapered roller bearings), the brake discs (although there are only three per axle, versus four on the TGV), and crash energy management techniques to control structural deformation in the event of an accident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trainweb1_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-trainweb1-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perren.2C_Brian_p156_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Perren.2C_Brian_p156-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tilting carriages are based upon Bombardier's earlier <a href="/wiki/LRC_(train)" title="LRC (train)">LRC</a> trains used on <a href="/wiki/Via_Rail" title="Via Rail">Via Rail</a> rather than the TGV's non-tilting articulated trailers. Acela power cars and passenger cars are much heavier than those of the TGV in order to meet the FRA's crash standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCaughrin.2C_Eric_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCaughrin.2C_Eric-56">[56]</a></sup> French and Canadian crews testing the Acela referred to it as "the fast pig" due to its weight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philips2010_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-philips2010-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The extra weight leads to the Acela's power-to-weight ratio being about 22.4 hp per tonne, compared to 30.8 hp for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SNCF_TGV_Reseau" title="SNCF TGV Reseau">SNCF TGV Reseau</a> trainset.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perren.2C_Brian_p156_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-Perren.2C_Brian_p156-54">[54]</a></sup> The Tier II crash standards, adopted in 1999, have also resulted in the passenger cars being designed without steps and trapdoors, which means that the trainsets can only serve lines with <a href="/wiki/Railway_platform_height" title="Railway platform height">high-level platforms</a> such as the Northeast Corridor. Acela trains are semi-permanently coupled (but not articulated as in the TGV) and are referred to as trainsets. <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a> later used the Acela carriage design and a <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gas_turbine" title="Gas turbine">gas turbine</a> variant of the power car for its experimental <a href="/wiki/JetTrain" title="JetTrain">JetTrain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Acela_trains">New Acela trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: New Acela trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Avelia_Liberty" title="Avelia Liberty">Avelia Liberty</a></div>
<p>On August 26, 2016, Vice President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> announced a $2.45 billion federal loan package to pay for new <i>Acela</i> equipment, as well as upgrades to the NEC. The loans will finance 28 train-sets that will replace the existing fleet. Amtrak will pay off the loans from increased NEC passenger revenue. The new trains will be called <a href="/wiki/Avelia_Liberty" title="Avelia Liberty">Avelia Liberty</a>. They will have one-third greater seating capacity, <a href="/wiki/Tilting_train" title="Tilting train">active tilt</a> technology and could operate at 186 miles per hour (299 km/h) if infrastructure improvements were completed to allow the higher speeds. The trains will be built by <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hornell,_New_York" title="Hornell, New York">Hornell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester, New York</a>. The new trains will be phased in between 2021 and 2022, after which the current fleet is to be retired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_speeds">Operating speeds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Operating speeds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With a 71:23 gear ratio, the Acela is designed with a top speed of 165 mph (266 km/h) and reaches a maximum speed of 150 mph (241 km/h) in regular service on three sections of track totaling 33.9 mi (55 km) in <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amtrakETT_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-amtrakETT-61">[61]</a></sup> The <i>Acela</i> achieves an average speed (including stops) of 81.7 mph (131 km/h) between Washington and New York,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-formw4_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-formw4-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-formw2_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-formw2-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and an average speed of 66.9 mph (108 km/h) from Washington to Boston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The average speed from New York to Boston is a slightly faster 69.8 mph (112 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg/220px-Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg/330px-Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg/440px-Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Acela_Express_and_Metro-North_railcar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An Acela Express train passes a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro-North" title="Metro-North">Metro-North</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Haven_Line" title="New Haven Line">New Haven Line</a> train in southwestern <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Amtrak also upgraded the track along the Connecticut shoreline east of New Haven to allow maximum speeds in excess of 110 mph (177 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> West of New York City, the Acela's top speed is 135 mph (217 km/h). One limiting factor is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overhead_catenary" title="Overhead catenary">overhead catenary</a> support system which was constructed before 1935 and lacks the constant-tension features of the new catenary east of New Haven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012update_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-2012update-6">[6]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Railroad" title="Pennsylvania Railroad">Pennsylvania Railroad</a> ran <i><a href="/wiki/Metroliner_(train)" title="Metroliner (train)">Metroliner</a></i> test trains in the late 1960s as fast as 164 mph (264 km/h) and briefly intended to run the <i>Metroliner</i> service at speeds reaching 150 mph (241 km/h). Certification testing for commercial operation at 160 mph (257 km/h) involving test runs at up to 165 mph (266 km/h) began between Trenton and New Brunswick in September 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aug-sept-2012-ink_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-aug-sept-2012-ink-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The slowest section of the electrified NEC is the portion owned by <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">Metro-North Railroad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Department_of_Transportation" title="Connecticut Department of Transportation">Connecticut Department of Transportation</a> between New Haven, Connecticut and <a href="/wiki/New_Rochelle,_New_York" title="New Rochelle, New York">New Rochelle, New York</a> and is heavily used by commuter trains. Amtrak's trains here achieve 90 mph (145 km/h) only on a limited 4-mile (6.4 km) stretch in New York State and rarely exceed 60 mph (97 km/h) at any time eastbound through Connecticut until reaching New Haven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In 1992, ConnDOT began plans to upgrade the catenary system,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> replace outdated bridges, and straighten certain sections of the New Haven Line to enable the <i>Acela</i> to run slightly faster. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the catenary replacement and bridge work were under way and expected to be completed in 2015. Curve straightening was deemed too expensive, and there are no current plans to increase speeds on the New Haven Line.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (December 2016)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On July 9, 2007, Amtrak introduced a limited-stop round trip, with trains stopping only at Philadelphia between New York and Washington. This shortened the trip between the two cities to 2 hours 35 minutes, making the trip roughly an hour faster than some of the <i><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Regional" title="Northeast Regional">Northeast Regional</a></i> train services. These trains were an experiment to find ways to expedite travel time on the Acela; Amtrak has since dropped them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amtrak_Northeast_Corridor_1_train_schedule_effective_August_4.2C_2008_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amtrak_Northeast_Corridor_1_train_schedule_effective_August_4.2C_2008-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_speed_infrastructure">High speed infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: High speed infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The dense population of the northeastern United States makes the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a> the most heavily traveled portion of the American passenger rail system. <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_New_York_City" title="Transportation in New York City">Two-thirds of rail passengers in the United States live in or near New York City</a>, also home to the nation's busiest passenger rail station, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Station_(New_York_City)" title="Pennsylvania Station (New York City)">Penn Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In order to compete with <a href="/wiki/Airliner" title="Airliner">airliners</a>, Amtrak needed to increase the speed of trains in the region. The former <a href="/wiki/Shore_Line_Railway_(Connecticut)" title="Shore Line Railway (Connecticut)">Shore Line</a>, from New Haven to Boston, is burdened by sharp turns and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grade_crossing" title="Grade crossing">grade crossings</a>, the crossings being of special concern.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tilting_train" title="Tilting train">Tilting</a> enables passengers to ride more comfortably on curved sections of track faster than would otherwise be possible, by leaning into the bend. Acela trainsets tilt above 60 mph (97 km/h) on most of the system, but some segments of track in the Northeast Corridor are too close together for the cars to safely tilt while maintaining <a href="/wiki/Federal_Railroad_Administration" title="Federal Railroad Administration">FRA</a> minimum space between trains on parallel tracks. Metro-North Railroad restricts tilting on the segment of track north of New York which it owns. The system was originally designed for a 6.8° tilt, but the cars were redesigned 4 in (10 cm) wider to accommodate wider seats and aisles that reduced allowable tilt to 4.2° to fit within the clearance constraints of the existing tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Railfan_Europe_Acela_Article_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Railfan_Europe_Acela_Article-74">[74]</a></sup> Traveling at higher than 135 mph (217 km/h) also requires constant-tension catenary, which is only implemented on the more modern catenary system north of New York City. South of New York City the trains are restricted to 135 mph (217 km/h). By comparison, Northeast Regional and the now-defunct <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metroliner_(Amtrak)" title="Metroliner (Amtrak)">Metroliner</a> service reached 125 mph (201 km/h).</p>
<p>Acela service was originally expected to begin in late 1999 but was delayed. The catenary system could not support the intended speeds between Washington DC and New York City, but the newer system between New York City and Boston allows the higher speeds. Attention was drawn to the decreased 4.2° tilt, but this was not the root of the speed problem, as the tracks from New York to Boston are similar to those between New York and Washington, and the tilt mechanism is not the factor enabling higher speeds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTtimeli_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-NYTtimeli-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Railfan_Europe_Acela_Article_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Railfan_Europe_Acela_Article-74">[74]</a></sup> Following repairs, the first Acela service began on December 11, 2000, a year behind schedule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the completion of electrification between New Haven and Boston, all trains on the line have become faster partly because of the removal of a 10‑minute delay in New Haven while swapping diesel and electric locomotives, partly from a faster acceleration away from station stops enabled by electric locomotives and partly because of the faster speed achieved on some sections of track. Acela travels between Boston and New York in about three and a half hours (an improvement of half an hour); New York to Washington runs take two hours and forty-five minutes. These schedules, as well as the relative convenience of rail as opposed to air travel especially after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">September 11, 2001 attacks</a>, and direct downtown-to-downtown service have made the Acela Express more competitive with the <a href="/wiki/Air_shuttle" title="Air shuttle">air shuttles</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Platform_track_speeds">Platform track speeds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Platform track speeds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Acela trains do not pass platforms of local stations at high speeds except in two locations. At <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingston_Railroad_Station_(Rhode_Island)" title="Kingston Railroad Station (Rhode Island)">Kingston Station</a> in Rhode Island, the trains pass platforms at 150 mph (241 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mansfield_(MBTA_station)" title="Mansfield (MBTA station)">Mansfield station</a> in Massachusetts, which also serves <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Bay_Transportation_Authority" title="Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority">MBTA</a> <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter rail</a>, has two platform tracks which are also used by Acela at 120 mph (193 km/h).</p>
<p>Concerns over inadequate warnings and safeguards have included that the two-foot wide yellow <a href="/wiki/Railway_platform#Markings" title="Railway platform">platform markings</a> may not keep people at a safe distance as trains pass at high speed. Suggestions include platform <a href="/wiki/Safety_barrier" title="Safety barrier">safety barriers</a>, or use of different announcements for approaching Acela trains versus slower ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2011, federal transportation grants were awarded to improve Kingston station, including the construction of a third track to be used by the Acela as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Through_track" title="Through track">through track</a> to bypass the station, helping to alleviate safety concerns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outages">Outages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Outages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In August 2002, shortly after their introduction, <i>Acela</i> trainsets were briefly removed from service when the brackets that connected truck (<a href="/wiki/Bogie" title="Bogie">bogie</a>) dampers (shocks) to the powerunit carbodies ("yaw dampers") were found to be cracking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The Acela returned to service when a program of frequent inspections was instituted. The damper brackets have since been redesigned and old brackets replaced by the newer design.</p>
<p>On April 15, 2005, the <i>Acela</i> was removed from service when cracks were found in the <a href="/wiki/Disc_brake" title="Disc brake">disc brakes</a> of many passenger coaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier</a>-<a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a> consortium replaced the discs under warranty. Limited service resumed in July 2005, as a portion of the fleet operated with new brake discs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metroliner_(Amtrak)" title="Metroliner (Amtrak)">Metroliner</a></i> trains, which the <i>Acela Express</i> was intended to replace, filled in during the outage. Amtrak announced on September 21, 2005, that all 20 trainsets had been returned to full operation.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Service">Service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amtrak_acela.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2365" data-file-width="3041" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Amtrak_acela.png/300px-Amtrak_acela.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Amtrak_acela.png/450px-Amtrak_acela.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Amtrak_acela.png/600px-Amtrak_acela.png 2x" width="300"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The production sets are formed as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">

<p>The <i>Acela Express</i> trainset consists of two <a href="/wiki/Power_car" title="Power car">power cars</a>, a café car, a First Class car, and four Business Class cars, semi-permanently coupled together. It has fewer seats than regional service counterparts. The First Class car has 44 seats, being three seats across (one on one side, two on the other side) and four seat tables. There are 260 Business Class seats on each trainset; these cars have four seats across (two on each side) and four-seat tables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-specs-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title=" Dead link since April 2014">dead link</span></a></i>]</span></sup> Reservations guarantee seating but seats are not assigned. Baggage may be stowed in overhead compartments or underneath seats. Trains are wheelchair-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accessible" title="Accessible">accessible</a>. Cars have one or two toilets each, with one ADA compliant.</p>
<p>The car adjacent to First Class is designated as the quiet car, where passengers are asked to refrain from loud talking and phone conversations. Automatic sliding doors between cars reduce noise.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Staffing_and_operation">Staffing and operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Staffing and operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(December 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Generally Amtrak train crews consist of an engineer, a conductor, and at least one assistant conductor. <i>Acela</i> trains also have an On-Board Service crew consisting of two First Class attendants and a Cafe Car attendant. In addition to the food service provided in the Cafe Car, on most trains an attendant will also provide at seat cart service, serving refreshments throughout the train. First Class passengers are served meals at their seats on all services.</p>
<p>At Amtrak, the On-Board Service crew is considered separate and subordinate to the Train and Engine crews. Acela maintenance is generally taken care of at the Ivy City facility in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington,_DC" title="Washington, DC">Washington, DC</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sunnyside_Yard" title="Sunnyside Yard">Sunnyside Yard</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queens,_New_York" title="Queens, New York">Queens, New York</a>; or <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Southampton_Street_Yard&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Southampton Street Yard (page does not exist)">Southampton Street Yard</a> in Boston.</p>
<p>The Acela trainsets underwent minor refurbishments between mid-2009 and 2010 at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Penn_Coach_Yard&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Penn Coach Yard (page does not exist)">Penn Coach Yard</a>, next to 30th Street Station in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia, Pennsylvania</a>. These refurbishments included new blue leather seats throughout the trainset.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wi-Fi_service">Wi-Fi service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Wi-Fi service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Wireless Internet station service began in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In 2010, all <i>Acela</i> trains began offering AmtrakConnect<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amtrak_Launches_Wi-Fi_Service_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amtrak_Launches_Wi-Fi_Service-87">[87]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Service_set_(802.11_network)" title="Service set (802.11 network)">SSID</a> AmtrakConnectAcela) supporting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/802.11" title="802.11">802.11</a> a/b/g/n, 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz and standard <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VPN" title="VPN">VPN</a> connections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amtrak_Launches_Wi-Fi_Service_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Amtrak_Launches_Wi-Fi_Service-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_incidents">Notable incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Acela_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notable incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first <i>Acela</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grade_crossing" title="Grade crossing">grade-crossing</a> accident occurred on September 27, 2005, when a car rolled under closed crossing gate arms in <a href="/wiki/Waterford,_Connecticut" title="Waterford, Connecticut">Waterford, Connecticut</a>, and was struck by a train traveling at 70 miles per hour (110 km/h), killing three. The gates were found to have been functioning properly,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-High-Tech_Gates_Fail_to_Avert_Car-Train_Crash_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-High-Tech_Gates_Fail_to_Avert_Car-Train_Crash-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Investigators_Seek_Answers_In_Fatal_Crash_That_Killed_Two.3B_Cause_of_Waterford_car-train_accident_may_never_be_known_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Investigators_Seek_Answers_In_Fatal_Crash_That_Killed_Two.3B_Cause_of_Waterford_car-train_accident_may_never_be_known-89">[89]</a></sup> but the incident drew much criticism regarding the eleven remaining grade crossings along Amtrak's busy Northeast Corridor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Family_sues_over_fatal_car_crash_on_railroad_tracks_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Family_sues_over_fatal_car_crash_on_railroad_tracks-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amtrak_train.2C_car_collide.2C_killing_two_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amtrak_train.2C_car_collide.2C_killing_two-91">[91]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-philips2010-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-philips2010_57-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Philips, Don (January 2010). "Now it seems to be official: Freight rail is the future". <i>Trains</i>. <b>70</b> (1): 10. <q>When the train was being tested at the technology center in Pueblo, Colo., I had lunch one day out on the ballast with the French and Canadian crews doing the testing. The conversation turned to the weight of the Acela, which the crews considered laughably too heavy. At one point, a French engineer confided that the crews called the train "le cochon", meaning "the pig". The man and his supervisor immediately realized he had said too much. They asked me to keep that a secret, and I did for many years until I was sure everyone on the program had moved on to other jobs.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAcela+Express&amp;rft.atitle=Now+it+seems+to+be+official%3A+Freight+rail+is+the+future&amp;rft.aufirst=Don&amp;rft.aulast=Philips&amp;rft.date=2010-01&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.jtitle=Trains&amp;rft.pages=10&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=70"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-58">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">James Dao; Matthew L. Wald; Don Philips (April 24, 2005). <a class="external text" href="http://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html?res=9506EEDB1531F937A15757C0A9639C8B63" rel="nofollow">"Acela, Built to Be Rail's Savior, Bedevils Amtrak at Every Turn"</a>. The New York Times. <q>Before the first train was built, the Federal Railroad Administration required it to meet crash safety standards that senior Amtrak officials considered too strict. That forced the manufacturers, Bombardier Inc. of Canada and GEC Alstom of France, to make the trains twice as heavy as European models. Workers dubbed the trains <i>le cochon</i> -- the pig.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAcela+Express&amp;rft.atitle=Acela%2C+Built+to+Be+Rail%27s+Savior%2C+Bedevils+Amtrak+at+Every+Turn&amp;rft.au=Don+Philips&amp;rft.au=James+Dao&amp;rft.au=Matthew+L.+Wald&amp;rft.date=2005-04-24&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fquery.nytimes.com%2Fgst%2Ffullpage.html%3Fres%3D9506EEDB1531F937A15757C0A9639C8B63&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a class="external text" href="http://findarticles.com/p/articles/mi_m0BQQ/is_11_42/ai_99569317/" rel="nofollow">"Bombardier unveils new JetTrain locomotive"</a>. <i>International Railway Journal</i>. <li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-60">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Aratani, Lori (August 26, 2016). <a class="external text" href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/dr-gridlock/wp/2016/08/26/biden-announces-upgrades-for-amtraks-northeast-corridor/" rel="nofollow">"Biden announces upgrades for Amtrak's Northeast Corridor"</a>. <i>Washington Post</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAcela+Express&amp;rft.atitle=Biden+announces+upgrades+for+Amtrak%99s+Northeast+Corridor&amp;rft.aufirst=Lori&amp;rft.aulast=Aratani&amp;rft.date=2016-08-26&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.washingtonpost.com%2Fnews%2Fdr-gridlock%2Fwp%2F2016%2F08%2F26%2Fbiden-announces-upgrades-for-amtraks-northeast-corridor%2F&amp;rft.jtitle=Washington+Post&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-amtrakETT-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-amtrakETT_61-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160203171230/http://dms.ntsb.gov/public/58000-58499/58167/585182.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Northeast Corridor Employee Timetable #5"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. National Railroad Passenger Corporation (Amtrak). 6 October 2014. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://dms.ntsb.gov/public/58000-58499/58167/585182.pdf" rel="nofollow">the original</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span> on February 3, 2016 – via National Transportation Safety Board.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAcela+Express&amp;rft.btitle=Northeast+Corridor+Employee+Timetable+%235&amp;rft.date=2014-10-06&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fdms.ntsb.gov%2Fpublic%2F58000-58499%2F58167%2F585182.pdf&amp;rft.pub=National+Railroad+Passenger+Corporation+%28Amtrak%29&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The timetable gives 2 hours and 45 minutes, minimum, between New York and Washington. Dividing that into 224.7 miles (361.6 km) (89.0 miles from New York Penn Station to Philadelphia + 134.6 to Washington, DC + 1.1 to Washington's Union Station) gives 81.7 mph.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-63">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The timetable gives 3 hours and 25 minutes, minimum, between Boston and New York. Dividing that into 228.7 route miles gives 66.9 mph.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-64">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The timetable gives 6 hours and 30 minutes, minimum. Dividing that into 464.5 route miles (228.7 miles Boston South Station to New York Penn Station + 224.7 to Washington Union Station) gives 69.75 mph.</span></li>
